тАШрд░рдпрд┐рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡реИрдкрджрдордзреНрдпрдпрдирддрдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд░реНрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдкрд░рд╛рд╢рд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдорд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдореН ред рдЕрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдЪ –тАЩ рд░рдпрд┐рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

66
Agni
Par─Б┼Ыara ┼Ъ─Бktya
10 verses: dvipad─Б vir─Бj
Like the previous hymn, this one is constructed of short phrases often consisting of similes. The similes here alternate between images of peace and prosperity and those of turbulent combat, sometimes strikingly juxtaposed, as in the second half of verse 3 or the contrasting halves of verse 4.
Toward the end of the hymn we find several puzzles, which have elicited widely differing interpretationsтАФespecially verse 8 with its double mention of twins (yam├б). In our view the end of the hymn builds toward a ritual climax, found in the final two verses of the hymn (9тАУ10), and verse 8 sets the stage for this, the early-morning sacrifice, by mentioning the risen sun as the twin already born and the soma, not yet pressed, as the twin awaiting birthтАФboth also identified with Agni. Although these identifications would break the pattern of constant refer
ence to Agni set in the earlier parts of the hymn (and our interpretation therefore gives us pause), the final pair of verses also move beyond the stasis of repeated Agni-similes and depict a ritual moment, prefigured, in our view, by the mention of other ritual entities in verse 8.
Note the ring-compositional element, the тАЬsight of the sun,тАЭ in the first half of verse 1 and the last words of verse 10. This double mention may support our inter pretation of verse 8 as mentioning the risen sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ[1-2] Agni who is like wondrous wealth, like the all-surveying Sun, like vital breath, like a well-conducted son, like a rider-bearing steed, like a milk-yielding cow, who is pure and radiant, consumes the forests.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Glittering like wealth, like the sight of the sun,
like life-breath, like oneтАЩs own son;

Jamison Brereton Notes

The fem. gender of citr─Б╠Бis a problem. The standard solution (see, e.g., Grassmann) is to assume that ray├н-, which is normally masc., is occasionally fem. (so also, supposedly, in nearby I.68.7, though see disc. there). I find this unsatisfactory and explain the gender by assuming that citr─Б╠Бmodifies not only ray├нс╕е but also fem.

saс╣Гdс╣Ы╠Бk and agrees with the latter.

Grassmann takes s┼л╠Бraс╕е as the nom. sg. of the thematic stem s┼л╠Бra-; in this he is apparently followed by Renou: тАЬ(propre ├а la) vision (des hommes) comme le soleil.тАЭ I find this unlikely, since saс╣Гdс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы- regularly takes the gen., incl. s┼л╠Бryasya (II.33.1, X.37.6, X.59.5). I therefore take s┼л╠Бraс╕е as gen. of sv├аr-, with, apparently, Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н).

More problematic is ─Б╠Бyur n├б pr─Бс╣З├бс╕е, where the first word should be the neut.

noun ─Б╠Бyus- тАШlifetimeтАЩ, since GrassmannтАЩs supposed adjectival stem ─Б╠Бyu- тАШbeweglichтАЩ does not exist (only the neut. noun ─Б╠Бyu-, also тАШlifetimeтАЩ). Thus, properly speaking, we should have an equational simile тАЬbreath like lifetime,тАЭ represented in RenouтАЩs тАЬsouffle-anim├й comme la vie (m├кme)тАЭ and Witzel Got┼Н тАЬder Atem gleichsam als Leben.тАЭ Nonetheless I consider the interpretation as an improper compound, as in GeldnerтАЩs тАЬwie der Lebenshauch,тАЭ to make more sense.

Like a swift bird, a cow who yields her milk, pure and refulgent to the wood he speeds.

Jamison Brereton

Like a swooping (bird), ever restless, he clings to the wood;
like a milk-cow (yielding) milk, (he is) blazing and widely radiant.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both t├бkvan- and bh┼л╠Бrс╣Зi- have received diverse tr., which I will not treat in detail here. For тИЪtak as тАШplunge, rushтАЩ, etc., see EWA s.v. TAK; here and in takva-v─л╠Б- I take it to refer to a тАЬswoopingтАЭ bird of prey. As for bh┼л╠Бrni, it belongs to тИЪbhur тАШquiverтАЩ, and I tr. it here as тАШrestlessтАЩ to capture the constant circling and diving of birds of prey. How then can he тАШclingтАЩ (siс╣гakti) to the wood? The image must be of the flames of the fire constantly licking and dancing (to use our preferred metaphors in English), but always in contact with the wood. My тАЬclingsтАЭ is a more vivid version of the literal тАЬaccompanies, keeps company with.тАЭ To avoid the appearance of contradiction, the phrase might better have been rendered тАЬever restless, like a swooping (bird), he (yet) clings to the wood.тАЭ Note that the second syllable of v├бn─Б somewhat echoes the n├б simile markers of previous p─Бdas.

The simile of c is syntactically problematic, consisting of a neut. NA sg.

p├бyaс╕е тАШmilkтАЩ and a fem. nom. sg. dhen├║с╕е тАШmilk-cowтАЩ, with the relation between them unspecified. Geldner simply takes it as a functional compound (тАЬwie die KuhmilchтАЭ), though unlike тАЬlife-breathтАЭ in 1c, the order of the elements would be wrong; Renou takes dhen├║с╕е as if it were gen. (тАЬcomme le lait (de) la vache-laiti├иreтАЭ), while Oldenberg (SBE) and Witzel Got┼Н render it as two similes (Oldenberg тАЬlike milk, like a milch-cowтАЭ). I have supplied a verb тАЬ(yielding),тАЭ allowing p├бyaс╕е to serve as acc. object, on the basis of IV.57.2 dhen├║r iva p├бyaс╕е … dhukс╣гva. None of these solutions is immediately satisfying. One clue might be whether the adjectives in d (┼Ы├║cir vibh─Б╠Бv─Б тАШblazing/gleaming and тАШfarradiantтАЩ) are applicable to either the one or the other of the nouns in the simile, but this doesnтАЩt turn out to be very helpful. Although both adjectives are regularly used of Agni, they are characteristic of neither milk nor cows. One exception is V.1.3 ┼Ы├║cir aс╣Еkte ┼Ы├║cibhir g├│bhir agn├нс╕е тАЬblazing Agni is anointed with blazing cows,тАЭ but there the тАЬcowsтАЭ stand for products of the cow, either milk (so the published translation) or, more likely, ghee, so that a metaphorical application to either noun is possible. And it may be that the simile in c is to be taken by itself, detached from the adjectives in d; see, e.g., 3cd, where the two p─Бdas, one a simile, the other not, are semantically independent.

Griffith

He offers safety like a pleasant home, like ripened corn, the Conqueror of men.
Like a Seer lauding, famed among the folk; like a steed friendly he vouchsafes us power.

Like unto a quick takvan 1 he (Agni) holds the wood, like milk, like a milch cow 2, bright and shining.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ[3-4] Like a secure mansion, he proects property; he (nourishes people) like barley; he is the conqueror of (hostile)) men; he is like a с╣Ыс╣гi, the praiser (of the gods), eminent amongst (devout) person ns; as a spirited horse (goes to battle), he repairs delighted to the hall of sacrifice; may be bestow upon us food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Delightful like a home, he maintains peace;
ripe like grain, a conqueror of peoples.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Renou notes, we might expect suffix-accented jet─Б╠Бwith gen. j├бn─Бn─Бm. Witzel Got┼Н, following Tichy (1995: 343-44), interpret the gen. in datival function (тАЬals Sieger f├╝r die MenschenтАЭ) to avoid nominal rection with a root-accented agent noun. But since this accentual тАЬruleтАЭ is often broken, I see no problem with the standard interpr. as objective gen. тАЬconquerer of peoples.тАЭ

Griffith

With flame insatiate, like eternal might; caring for each one like a dame at home;
Bright when he shines forth, whitish mid the folk, like a car, gold-decked, thundering to the fight.

He holds safety, pleasant like a homestead, like ripe barley, a conqueror of men,

рдкреНрд░рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрдГ рд╡рд╛рдЬреА рди рдЕрд╢реНрд╡ рдЗрд╡ рдкреНрд░реАрддрдГ рд╣рд░реНрд╖рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ ред рдпрдерд╛рд╢реНрд╡реЛ рд╣рд░реНрд╖рдпреБрдХреНрддреЛ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреНрдирдирд╛рдоред тАШ рд╡рдпрдГ рдХреНрд╖рджреНрдо’ рдЗрддрд┐ рддрдиреНрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН рее рджрд╛рдзрд╛рд░ ред рддреБрдЬрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрд░реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрддреБрд╕реБ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдордиреН ред рдирд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рд░рдгреНрд╡рдГ ред тАШ рд░рд╡рд┐ рдзрд╡рд┐ Jamison Brereton

Having rhythm like a seer, lauded among the clans;
well treated like a winning horse, he confers vitality.

Griffith

He strikes with terror like a dart shot forth, e’en like an archer’s arrow tipped with flame;
Master of present and of future life, the maidens’ lover and the matrons’ Lord.

Oldenberg

Like a Rishi uttering (sacred) shouts, praised among the clans; like a well-cared-for race-horse 1, Agni bestows vigour.

Geldner

lobsingend wie ein Rishi, unter allen V├╢lkern gefeiert, wie ein freudiges Streitro├Я leiht er die Kraft.

Grassmann

Behagen schafft er, тАУ hold wie ein Wohnhaus, wie reife Gerste, тАУ der M├дnner Sieger, Wie S├дnger rauschend, тАУ ger├╝hmt bei Menschen, wie lieber Renner тАУ verschafft er Labung.

рдлрд┐рд░ рд╡рд╣ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдХреИрд╕рд╛ рд╣реЛ, рдпрд╣ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп (рдУрдХрдГ) рдШрд░ рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд░рдгреНрд╡рдГ) рд░рдордгреАрдпрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк (рдкрдХреНрд╡рдГ) рдкрдХреЗ (рдпрд╡рдГ) рд╕реБрдЦ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдпрд╡ рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди (рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ) рдордиреНрддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд╕реНрддреБрднреНрд╡рд╛) рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рд╡рд╛рдЬреА) рд╡реЗрдЧрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдШреЛреЬреЗ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рдкреНрд░реАрддрдГ) рдХрдордиреАрдп (рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБ) рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрдд) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда (рдЬрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЖрджрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЬреЗрддрд╛) рд╕реБрдЦ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдЬреАрд╡рди (рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣ (рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордореН) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХреЛ (рджрд╛рдзрд╛рд░) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рее реи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЬреАрд╡рди рдХреЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрдд рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХрд╛рдо рдХреА рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдЬрд╛рдирдХреЗ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд┐рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ рдЖрд╣рд╛рд░ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░ рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдпрдерд╛рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рдмрд╣реБрдд рдХрд╛рд▓ рдкрд░реНрдпрдиреНрдд рдЬреА рдХреЗ рд╕рджрд╛ рд╕реБрдЦреА рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее реи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдУрдХреЛ рдиреЗрд╡ рд░рдгреНрд╡рдГ рдкрдХреНрд╡реЛ рдпрд╡реЛ рдиреЗрд╡ рдкрдХреНрд╡рдЛрд╖рд┐рд░реНрдиреЗрд╡ рд╕реНрддреБрднреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЬреА рдиреЗрд╡ рдкреНрд░реАрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддреЛ рдЬрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЬреЗрддрд╛ рд╡рдпреЛ рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐ рд╕ рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордВ рджрд╛рдзрд╛рд░ рее реи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдГ рдХреАрджреГрд╢реЛ рднрд╡реЗрджрд┐рддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджрд╛рдзрд╛рд░) рдзрд░реЗрддреНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рддреБрдЬрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рджреАрд░реНрдШреЛрд╜рднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдГред (рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордореН) рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдХрд░рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН (рдУрдХрдГ) рдЧреГрд╣рдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд░рдгреНрд╡рдГ) рд░рдордгреАрдпрдГ (рдпрд╡рдГ) рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд╛рд░реА рдзрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдкрдХреНрд╡рдГ) рдЙрдкрднреЛрдХреНрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рдГ (рдЬреЗрддрд╛) рдЙрддреНрдХрд░реНрд╖рддреНрд╡рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХрдГ (рдЬрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдореН (рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ) рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдХрдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд╕реНрддреБрднреНрд╡рд╛) рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдХрдГред рд╕реНрддреЛрднрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдЪрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрей.резрек) (рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБ) рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрдирд╛рд╕реБ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реБ (рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдГ) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардГ (рд╡рд╛рдЬреА) рд╡реЗрдЧрд╡рд╛рдирд╢реНрд╡рдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдкреНрд░реАрддрдГ) рдХрдордиреАрдпрдГ (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореН (рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐) рдзрд░реЗрддреН рее реи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

Sayana bhashya empty

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ[5-6] Agni of unattainable brightness, is like a vigilant sacrificer; he is an ornament to all (in the sacrificial chamber), like a woman in a dwelling; when he shines with wonderful lustre, he is like the white (sun) or like a golden chariot amongst men, resplendent in battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whose blaze is beyond domestication like oneтАЩs own will;
like a wife in the lap, enough for anyone.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The two halves of this verse are conceptually more complex than those preceding. Most tr. take a and b as implicitly contrastive: AgniтАЩs blaze is undomesticated but he is nonetheless intimately familiar – e.g., Geldner тАЬDessen Flamme schwer heimisch wird, (und doch ist er) eingeboren wie die Einsicht.тАЭ This is certainly possible. However, although I recognize the contrast between dur├│ka- and n├нtya-, I think the poet is equating the two elements in a clever play: AgniтАЩs flame canтАЩt be controlled and тАЬdomesticatedтАЭ anymore than a man in the grip of his own will.

As for the second half, I find it hard to believe that the poet is implying that oneтАЩs wife is at the disposition of everybody, with the distasteful sexual connotations this implies – as in RenouтАЩs тАЬ(se mettent) ├а disposition pour chacun comme lтАЩ├йpouse sur la couche.тАЭ Rather I think this is the Papageno situation: all it takes for anyone to be happy is his own wife in his lap.

Griffith

To him lead all your ways: may we attain the kindled God as cows their home at eve.
He drives the flames below as floods their swell: the rays rise up to the fair place of heaven.

Oldenberg

He to whose flame men do not grow accustomed 1, who is like one’s own mind 2, like a wife on a couch, enough for all (happiness).

Geldner

Dessen Flamme schwer heimisch wird, und doch ist er eingeboren wie die Einsicht, f├╝r jeden bereit wie die Frau auf dem Lager

Grassmann

Nicht leicht entz├╝ndbar, тАУ wie Kraft best├дndig, wie Frau im Hause тАУ bereit f├╝r jeden; Hell, wenn er aufstrahlt тАУ wie Licht in H├дusern, wie goldner Wagen тАУ in Schlachten eilend.

Jamison Brereton

When, glittering, he has flashed like a white (horse) among the clans, like a brilliant chariot (he is) dazzling in combats.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬhorseтАЭ generally supplied with ┼Ыvet├бс╕е тАШwhiteтАЩ is based on the regular cooccurrence of that adj. with ├б┼Ыva- and other expressions for тАШhorseтАЩ, including metaphorically of Agni (e.g., V.1.4). It of course also harmonizes nicely with the chariot of cd.

When the bright (Agni) has shone forth, he is like a white (horse [?]) 1 among people, like a chariot with golden ornaments, impetuous in fights.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

Sayana bhashya empty

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ[7-8] He terrifies (his adversaries) like an army sent (against an enemy), or like the bright-pointed shaft of an archer. Agni, as Yama, is all that is born; as Yama, all that will be born; he is the lover of maidens, the husband of wives.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yamo ha j─Бto, yamo janitvam: yama is interpreted as: yacchati dad─Бti k─Бm─Бn stotс╣Ыbhyaс╕е, he who gives the desired object to the worshippers; so, Yama becomes a synonym of Agni: yam agnir ucyate; or, Agni becomes one of the twins (yama), by the simultaneous birth of Indra and Agni (according to Y─Бska);

J─Бta = all existing beings;

Janitva = those that will exist; the terms imply dependence of all existence, past, present, or future, upon worship with fire; lover of maids: the essential part of the nuptial ceremony is completed when the maiden offers to fire; husband of wives: An allusion to a legend; Soma obtained a maiden and gave her to gandharva, Vi┼Ыv─Бvasu; he transferred her to Agni, who gave her to a mortal husband and bestowed upon her wealth and offspring; the reference is to the wife as a chief participant in the oblations to fire

Jamison Brereton

Set loose like an army, he initiates an onslaught,
like the arrow of an archer with its dazzling point.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the RV itтАЩs necessary to allow s├йn─Б- to mean both тАШarmyтАЩ and тАШweaponтАЩ; although the latter could make sense here (so Renou), an army is more likely to produce an onslaught than a single weapon.

Griffith

Jamison Brereton

(The one) twin [=Sun?] has been born, (the other) twin [=Soma?] is what is to be born:
(the one [=Sun]) is the lover of girls [=Dawns?]; (the other [=Soma]) the husband of women [=cowsтАЩ (milk)?].

Jamison Brereton Notes

As discussed in the published introduction, this verse is quite opaque and breaks the pattern of Agni-describing similes that has prevailed up to now in this hymn (and the last one). It has, not surprisingly, stimulated much discussion and some fanciful interpretations, all the details of which I will not rehearse here. The first question that must be addressed is what the first word (and the fourth), yam├бс╕е, represents here. Is it the PN Yama, naming the first man and the king of the dead? or the common noun тАШtwinтАЩ? or even the common noun тАШcontrollerтАЩ (though we might then expect the accent y├бma-)? What one decides about this question determines the direction of interpretation of the rest of the verse. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take it as Yama, here identified with Agni; Renou and Oldenberg (and I) as тАШtwinтАЩ, with the two twins displaying different characteristics. The rhetorical structure of the verse favors this interpretation; not only do the first two p─Бdas both begin yam├бс╕е, a repetition that invites (but does not require) a тАЬthe one тАж the other тАжтАЭ reading, but the contrastive characterizations found in cd also support it.

The next problem is the gender discrepancy between j─Бt├бс╕е (m.) and j├бnitvam (n.) in what appear to be parallel equational clauses. To solve this Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) simply supply a verb with the second, to which j├бnitvam serves as object: тАЬals Yama (erzeugt er) das k├╝nftiges Geschlecht.тАЭ But this would disturb the balanced structure of the verse, and it seems best to allow j├бnitvam to be predicated of yam├бс╕е, as Oldenberg and Renou (and I) do. Where I differ from these latter is in my interpretation of the two equations. Oldenberg and Renou take both twins to be identified with Agni, with each тАЬtwinтАЭ representing one aspect of AgniтАЩs nature. I think that each twin is identified first with another entity, which is then secondarily identified with Agni. Although this might seem complex, it allows the other parts of the verse to bear more meaning than the exclusive тАЬAgni = one twin, Agni = other twinтАЭ interpretation admits. As indicated in the published introduction, I take the verse as reflecting the circumstances of the early morning ritual, when the fire is kindled at sunrise and the soma is pressed for the first offering.

Under that interpretation the twin that has (already) been born (j─Бt├бс╕е) would be the sun, at whose appearance the ceremony gets started. The twin that is the substance to be born (j├бnitvam) would be the soma. The two are not only twins of each other, but each is the twin of Agni. Soma and the sun are not infrequently identified (see, e.g., IX.66.18 tv├бс╣Г soma s┼л╠Бra ├йс╣гaс╕е тАЬyou, Soma, are the sunтАЭ); the identification of Agni and the sun is a commonplace; and Agni can also be identified with Soma (see, e.g., the tс╣Ыca IX.66.19-21), and they frequently share epithets (like ┼Ы├║ci-, discussed above 2d, though in another context).

I then take the two p─Бdas cd as referring to the sun and the soma respectively.

The sun is тАЬthe lover of girlsтАЭ because he appears with the Dawns. For the same phrase, in the acc., referring (most probably) to the sun, see I.152.4. Whereas in IX.86.32 our same phrase p├бtir j├бn─лn─Бm is applied to Soma, where the тАЬwomen/wivesтАЭ are the milk-drinks with which he is mixed. As for the secondary reference to Agni, of these characterizations, either group of females (or both) might refer to the offering ladles (fem. juh┼л╠Б-) that approach the ritual fire with their oblations or the streams (fem. dh─Б╠Бr─Б-) of melted butter being offered. See the fem. pl.

n─л╠Бc─лс╕е in 10b.

Despite the complications of this interpretation, it provides a rich reading of the enigmatic verse, which fits well with the two ritually centered verses that end the hymn.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

Sayana bhashya empty

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ[9-10] Let us approach that blazing Agni with animal and vegetable offerings, as cows hasten to their stalls. He has tossed about his flames (in every direction), like running streams of water; the rays comingle (with the radiance) visible in the sky.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Caratha and vasthaya are explained as animal and vegetable offerings; further elaboration: tat prabh─Бvaiс╕е bс╣Ыday─Бdibhiс╕е s─Бdhy─Бhutiс╕е, pa┼Ыuprabh─Бva-hс╣Ыday─Бdis─Бdhan─Бy─Бhutya, these are invocations prompted by minds purified by offerings of moveable things, that is, animals; or of immoveable things, as rice, and the like

Jamison Brereton

With our movable (goods [=livestock]) and with our settled
household, we,
like cows (going) home, approach him, on your behalf, when he has been kindled.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, I consider the last two verses of the hymn to reflect the ritual situation. This scenario is supported by the presence of 1st and 2nd pronouns (vay├бm and vaс╕е respectively), with the 2nd ps. enclitic indicating, as often, the other human participants and observers besides the poet and priests, who are the тАЬwe.тАЭ The crux in this verse is car─Б╠Бth─Б. The first problem with it is the long ─Б in the 2nd syllable, the only instance of such a stem in the transmitted RV beside regularly formed car├бtha- (13x). However, the situation is more complex: 4 of the transmitted car├бtha- forms occur in the Par─Б┼Ыara hymns (I.68.1, 70.3, 7, 72.6), but of these, 3 (68.1, 70.3, 7) would be metrically better if read *car─Б╠Бtha-. I have no explanation for the variation and will not pursue the issue further. More interesting is the grammatical identity of the form and the semantic role it plays in the verse. Oldenberg (SBE, Noten) and Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take it as a nom. pl. тАШwanderersтАЩ, neuter if flg. the Pp., though Geldner suggests that it might reflect masc. car─Б╠Бth─Бс╕е. They further interpret it as conjoined with vay├бm (Oldenberg, Geldner) or identified with it (Witzel Got┼Н). However, in the Noten (ad loc., fn. 1) Oldenberg allows the possibility that the form could be an instr. parallel with vasaty─Б╠Б(тАЬmit Gehen und mit VerweilenтАЭ), an idea that Renou develops, suggesting that the pair are semantically parallel to the contrastive pair y├│ga / kс╣г├йma (roughly тАЬactivity and restтАЭ). Renou believes that the instrumentals characterize Agni (тАЬ(soit) dans (sa) marche, (soit) dans (sa) demeureтАЭ). This is possible, though it would be a slightly odd use of the instr. With Renou I consider car─Б╠Бth─Б an instr. contrasting with vasaty─Б╠Б, but think that the pair is applicable to тАЬusтАЭ: we approach Agni with homage with both our movable goods, that is, the livestock that provides the butter and milk offerings, and our household establishment that supplies the rest.

The 3rd pl. n├бkс╣гante (n├бkс╣гanta in sandhi) does not agree with its 1st pl. subject vay├бm. With Geldner I take it as attraction to the immediately preceding simile, ├бstaс╣Г n├б g─Б╠Бvaс╕е. It is accented because it begins the p─Бda.

Griffith

1 As cows go to their stalls, all that moves and we, for the sake of a dwelling, reach him who has been kindled.

Zu diesem eurem Agni kommen die Wanderer und wir mit der Hausgenossenschaft wie die K├╝he nach Hause, wenn er angez├╝ndet ist

Grassmann

Zu dem entflammten тАУ gehn eure Wege, in unser Haus wir тАУ wie heim die K├╝he; Wie Strom die Fluten тАУ trieb er herab sie, die K├╝he br├╝llten, тАУ wie Licht zu schauen.

Jamison Brereton

Like a river its gush, he has sent forth those [=butter offerings?] heading downward.
The cows cry out upon seeing the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The fem. pl. n─л╠Бc─лс╕е has almost too many possible referents – waters, flames, cows, or butter offerings (configured as cows) - all of which have been proposed by one or more tr. I favor butter offerings. See also VIII.101.13, also containing n─л╠Бc─л and showing the same range of possibilities; sim. V.44.4. The cows of c may well be the same offerings metaphorically.

See introduction. for the ring compositional final p─Бda. As Renou points out, sv├аr dс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы─лke is a nominalizing extension of the infinitive phrase sv├аr dr┼Ы╠е ├й тАЬto see the sun,тАЭ and we need not try to interpret sv├аr as a genitive.

Like the flood of the Sindhu 1 he has driven forward the downwards-flowing (waters) 2. The cows lowed at the sight of the sun 3.

Geldner

Grassmann

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддрдореН) рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрдореН (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рдЪрд░рд╛рдерд╛) рдЪрд░рд╛рдердпрд╛ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЪрд░рдзрд╛рддреЛ рдмрд╛рд╣реБрд▓рдХрд╛рджреМрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХреЛрд╜рдердкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╛рджреЗрд░реНрджреАрд░реНрдШрдГ рд╕реБрдкрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрд▓реБрдЧрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджреЗрд╢рд╢реНрдЪред (рд╡рдпрдореН) рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рддрд╛рд░рдГ (рд╡рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛) рд╡рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВ рддрдпрд╛ (рдЕрд╕реНрддрдореН) рдЧреГрд╣рдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ) рдкрд╛рд▓рд┐рддрд╛ рдзреЗрдирд╡рдГ (рдирдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдЗрджреНрдзрдореН) рджреАрдкреНрддрдореН (рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреБрдГ) рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдХреНрд╖реЛрджрдГ) рдЬрд▓рдореН (рдкреНрд░) рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ (рдиреАрдЪреАрдГ) рдирд┐рдореНрдирджреЗрд╢реЗ (рдРрдиреЛрддреН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдгреН рдзрд╛рддреЛрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рд╢реНрдиреБрдГред (рдирд╡рдиреНрдд) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ред рдирд╡рдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдЧрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежреи.резрек) (рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ) рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╛рдГ (рд╕реНрд╡рдГ) рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпреЗ (рджреГрд╢реАрдХреЗ) рджрд░реНрд╢рдХреЗред рдЕрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╢рдзрд╛рддреЛрд░реНрдмрд╛рд╣реБрд▓рдХрд╛рджреМрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХ рдИрдХрдиреН рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ рдХрд┐рдЪреНрдЪ рее рел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реМред рдп рдПрд╡рдВ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдВ рд╕рдВрд╕реЗрд╡реНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддрдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдиреН рдпрдерд╛ рдЧрд╛рд╡реЛ рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╛рдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рдЪ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдереИрд╡ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ред рдпрдерд╛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдГ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рдирд╛рдирд╛рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдгреНрдпрд▓рдВрдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ рддрдереИрд╡ рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрдиреИрд░рдиреНрддрд░реНрдпрд╛рдорд┐рдгрдореБрдкрд╛рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдХрд╛рдорд╛ рдЕрд▓рдВрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ рее рел рее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрд╢реНрдЪ рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН рее
